Supplementary Notes\n\n1 . Abstract\n6\n\nThe feasibility of using a scanning optical system to provide the attitude and trajectory\nof an unmanned spacecraft during an orbit about is investigated. It is assumed that the\nMars\n\nspacecraft is nearly attitude stabilized by a Sun-Canopus Tracking System. The scanning instrument\n\nyields\n\na\n\nmore\n\naccurate\n\ndetermination of\nits attitude by use of stellar detections across\n\nthree slits. The same slits occasionally detect transits of the Martian and these tranmoons,\nsits together with the stellar transits are sufficient to yield the trajectories of the moons\nand spacecraft as well\nIn the\n\nas\n\nthe\n\nhigher\n\nharmonic\n\ncoefficients\n\nof\n\nthe\n\nMartian\n\ngravitation\n\npotential.\n\ninvestigation, the accuracy with which the attitude, trajectories, and potential\n\ncan be determined from the measurements ik studied. Also, an analysis perturbations of\nof the\nthe spacecraft\'s position due to the moon\'s force fields is given. Finally, the instrument\ndetection problems are discussed and instrument design parameters are derived.\n\n17. Key Words (Suggested by Authodrt t\n\n18. Moons\n\nA method of computing the perturbationsby use of a linearization\nabout a single reference Kepler orbit was first developed. The resultant\nformula is given by equation ()\n5.\nHere an integration of an explicit\nfunction is required.\nNumerical results are given for thefollowing values of the\nunperturbed elements of the spacecraft\'s orbit:\n0\n\ni = 0\n\n, 40\xc2\xb0\n\na = 20415.5 km\n\ne = 078199\nTp= 0 hr\n\n0 5\n\nu)\n\n2 10\n8\'\n\n0 1 fi 5 360\xc2\xb0\n.\nSince asymmetry exists, all values of and\n\nn were studied.\n\n0\n\nResults for the case i = 40 are summarized on page 2 4 . A physical\nrationale is then given for these results. I is expected that these\nt\nresults may be generalized for\nall inclinations other than those near or\nequal to zero.\nFor inclinations at or near zero, a collision of the spacecraft\nand Phobos is possible under certain initial conditions. If initial\nconditions near these arechosen, long-track perturbationsresult which\nare positive or negative. A canceling effect is thus possible and does\noccur if the positive and negative yielding initial conditions occur\nrelatively near each other.\n\nThe results given can be generalized to other cases except those near\nresonance. That is, cases in which the ratio of the spacecraft\'s period\nto a moon\'s\nperiod is a rational fraction whose numerator and denominator\nare relatively small. For these cases, the perturbations grow large, and\nequation ( 5 ) may not be valid.\n\n121\n\nAvailabilityofthe\n\nMoons\n\nThe s t r o n g e s t s i n g l e f a c t o r w h i c h h i n d e r s t h e
